  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_874a0750-a1a4-4e69-863a-eee7f9c2befe'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer10845445436186933583">The holidays are over and Massie's room is chock-full of new things from Santa: jeans, sweater, and a new . . . roommate? Once Claire unpacks, Massie's room feels more crowded than a Zac Posen sample sale.   <span id="freeText10845445436186933583" style="display:none">The holidays are over and Massie's room is chock-full of new things from Santa: jeans, sweater, and a new . . . roommate? Once Claire unpacks, Massie's room feels more crowded than a Zac Posen sample sale. But what's worse, Claire isn't the only person moving into Massie's territory -- Alicia's hot cousin, Nina, shows up from Spain and starts edging in on all the Briarwood boys, including Massie's crush! Will Nina, with her super-tight mall clothes, make every boy in Westchester fall in love with her? Or will Massie toss her out faster than last season's Sevens jeans? The social minefields of Westchester County's most privileged middle school girls drive the page-turning action of this addictive series, set in New York City's most elite suburban county. The Clique . . . the only thing harder than getting in is staying in.<br /><b>Book Details:</b> 
   Format: Paperback 
   Publication Date: 10/5/2005 
   Pages: 256 
   Reading Level: Age 12 and Up

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2283835569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17882841139792828400">• i think this cover was my fav one. also i can’t rmr just how far i got in this series.<br/>• thinking more broadly abt YA of this era, i’m wondering what the equivalent trending genre was for young male readers. or how these wealth porn books would have been written for them at all.<br/>• this one feels extra mean spirited because it involves claire executing a scheme with no remorse. before this she usually had some reservations. all these mean girls are essentially the same— acting out in order to com</span>
  <span id="freeText17882841139792828400" style="display:none">• i think this cover was my fav one. also i can’t rmr just how far i got in this series.<br />• thinking more broadly abt YA of this era, i’m wondering what the equivalent trending genre was for young male readers. or how these wealth porn books would have been written for them at all.<br />• this one feels extra mean spirited because it involves claire executing a scheme with no remorse. before this she usually had some reservations. all these mean girls are essentially the same— acting out in order to compensate for their own insecurities— but we are led to believe that nina is different somehow.<br />• imagine a YA book with a school bomb threat joke in this day and age, lmao.<br />• this book revolves all around the girls getting their first kisses or whatever, but the boys here are such nonentities. at the heart of each girl’s romantic conflict is the fear that she is either undesirable by men or lagging behind in development. which is probably the most realistic part of the whole thing and contributes to my theory that this series is at the end of the day more abt youth becoming cognizant of the restraints of femininity. blah blah blah</span>
  <a data-text-id="17882841139792828400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

This book, actually this series, makes me want to either a.) vomit or b.) gouge my eyes out with a very pointy fork.<br/><br/>First, what the hell is the point to this book? Is it "I'm twelve years old and I run the school; if you don't listen to me, I'll ruin your life"? Or is it "I don't like her - let's destroy her life"? Seriously? I WAS a twelve year. I know no one, who acted like that. Sure, there were bitches; but seriously?<br/><br/>Second, the way Massie puts everyone down is really annoying. I </span>
  <span id="freeText5650867450741268400" style="display:none">Seriously? This book, actually this series, makes me want to either a.) vomit or b.) gouge my eyes out with a very pointy fork.<br /><br />First, what the hell is the point to this book? Is it "I'm twelve years old and I run the school; if you don't listen to me, I'll ruin your life"? Or is it "I don't like her - let's destroy her life"? Seriously? I WAS a twelve year. I know no one, who acted like that. Sure, there were bitches; but seriously?<br /><br />Second, the way Massie puts everyone down is really annoying. I want to smack some sense into her. She puts even her friends down, and thats just sad. There aren't any redeeming qualities about her.<br /><br />Third, the writing sucks. I'm not sure if it was the way the girls acted or if it was the writing that made me want to gouge my eyes out.<br /><br />The only redeeming thing to come out of this book is Claire, who still has some of her old personbalty and her friend Layne, but she still doesn't save the book.</span>

  <span id="freeText18086270082375885235" style="display:none"> In the fourth book of this series Claire and Massie are finally becoming friends, but the better friends they are, the more the other three hate them. The girls are excited about the Valentine's dance with all the Briarwood Boys... until Alici's hott new cousin moves in and starts to steal the boys hearts, and other things.(; I think this is a nice addition to the first three books in the series, but I think these books are really easy to read. Teenagers go through the same things as the OCD girls (boys, friendships, clothes, sports, ect.) but it seems like the books are at fourth grade reading level! I still read them though because they are fun! Lisi is a great author... but seems to make the girls in this book really stuck up. Massie and her Pretty Comittee only wear prada. I don't even own prada! I think thats where Claire comes in. She's the normal one that brings the girls back down to Earth. I like Lisi Harrison's style and I'm going to continue to read these books because they draw me in. Thats my favorite part about them, they are almost impossible to put down! She's definatley right about this though: The Clique... the only thing harder than getting in, is staying in!</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387868513" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11984694565593067852">It feels strange to rate a book I've outgrown five stars but this was my favorite of the series back in the old days, and for good reason. Childish as I see the storyline now, it's still somehow freaking hilarious.<br/><br/>Claire doesn't move (shocker) and the clique is happy as the day is long only for Alicia's cousin Nina to show up and quarrel with Massie. Sides are taken, some of the girls taking Nina's part initially despite their friendship with Massie. Then Nina (who is creepily over-sexed for a t</span>
  <span id="freeText11984694565593067852" style="display:none">It feels strange to rate a book I've outgrown five stars but this was my favorite of the series back in the old days, and for good reason. Childish as I see the storyline now, it's still somehow freaking hilarious.<br /><br />Claire doesn't move (shocker) and the clique is happy as the day is long only for Alicia's cousin Nina to show up and quarrel with Massie. Sides are taken, some of the girls taking Nina's part initially despite their friendship with Massie. Then Nina (who is creepily over-sexed for a thirteen year old) goes after their boyfriends and they get cheesed off and run back to Massie.<br /><br />Meanwhile Dylan catches the flu but is so frightened of missing the social scene at school she shows up whacked out on cold meds resulting in a hilarious scene during which she thinks she sees snakes wearing swim goggles and breaks down wailing, "Those are MY goggles, mine!"<br /><br />Later she shows up still sick at a school dance and talks about "Kristen's mom going off," but her stuffy nose makes it sound like "Kristen's BOMB." Wackiness ensues.<br /><br />Claire and Cam break up because he sees Claire kiss another guy, who happens to be Alicia's crush. <br /><br />Nina is revealed to have been a geek in the past.<br /></span>

          </span>

Love the character development of Massie and Claire in this book, and the ending is absolutely insane! I never expected Claire to kiss Josh AND have Cam see it. That’s juicy! </span>

<div id="review_54700192" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54700192" />
    <a title="Jazmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1621901-jazmine"><img alt="Jazmine" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/54700192?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jazmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jazmine" href="/user/show/1621901-jazmine">Jazmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Clique fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jazmine by: </span>
      I've been reading them
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54700192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9186470311008245813">Mr. Lyons received a job offer in Chicago, but no one wants the family to move away. Mr. Block promotes Mr. Lyons giving him enough money to give the guest house an extreme makeover. Until the house is done being built, the Lyons must live in the Block’s home. Claire is allergic to Bean, messes up all the clothes Massie lends her, cries loudly at night over losing Cam, and has a hard time getting a turn in the shower. They make a deal to make peace by having Claire sleep in the bath tub. All the</span>
  <span id="freeText9186470311008245813" style="display:none">Mr. Lyons received a job offer in Chicago, but no one wants the family to move away. Mr. Block promotes Mr. Lyons giving him enough money to give the guest house an extreme makeover. Until the house is done being built, the Lyons must live in the Block’s home. Claire is allergic to Bean, messes up all the clothes Massie lends her, cries loudly at night over losing Cam, and has a hard time getting a turn in the shower. They make a deal to make peace by having Claire sleep in the bath tub. All the while, Alicia’s flirtatious cousin Nina from Spain is stealing all of the girls’ crushes. Many look to Nina for boy and clothing advice including Kristen and Dylan, and Alicia, Massie, and Claire’s picks for the dance; Josh, “Derrington,” and Cam end up taking Nina to the dance instead of them like they were supposed to. It turns out that Nina is also a real thief as she has been taking a lot of people’s possessions. It takes a few operations and detentions until they finally find evidence, her stash of stolen items. At the Love Struck Dance when she Nina is awarded the Cupid Award with Derrington they completely humiliate and expose her. They had her heels sawed off so she trips, then Alicia reveals Nina’s stash of stolen items causing Nina to be bombarded by angry people, and old, ugly pictures of Nina are spread to everyone. Nina leaves America the very next day only to be welcomed by her furious, older sisters because Nina had taken their boots and such. They all go to the soccer finals and Derrington, the star goalie, gets hit in the face after Massie wishes he would be, so they most likely lose. Derrington asks Massie to meet him and she learns the reason why he’d avoided her is because Nina lied and said that they had to if they wanted to win the soccer game. She gives him an M brooch to remember her and he gives her the Cupid award that would’ve been given to her had Nina not forced him to come to the dance with her. Claire takes Massie’s advice and flirts with another boy, Josh, whom Alicia says she’s over. She ends up having her first kiss with him which Cam sees and is upset by. He had only avoided her because of Nina’s Spanish soccer spell which he though Claire knew about but she didn’t. <br /><br />	The characters were well developed as always, and I feel as though Claire is gaining confidence and a stronger relationship with Massie. Nina was a very interesting character and I thought the girls most definitely got their revenge at the end. I’m glad she’s gone because she was making everything complicated. I was shocked that Claire had kissed Josh and not Cam, too. I can’t wait to read the next book of course.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9186470311008245813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_168959212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168959212" />
    <a title="Lillie Mansour" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5055028-lillie-mansour"><img alt="Lillie Mansour" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298950875p2/5055028.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168959212?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lillie Mansour" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lillie Mansour" href="/user/show/5055028-lillie-mansour">Lillie Mansour</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168959212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13465598357320184505">This book is about a group of girls called the "Pretty Committee". They are the total "It Girls" of the school. The people in the Pretty Committee were Massie, Alicia, Dylan, Kristen, and the new girl Claire. They are all supposedly beautiful besides Claire. She wears ugly clothes, has greasy bangs that go straight across her forehead, and an awful since of fashion. Throughout the previous books, the Pretty Committee go on a and off with liking Claire. They are pretty much forced to be with her </span>
  <span id="freeText13465598357320184505" style="display:none">This book is about a group of girls called the "Pretty Committee". They are the total "It Girls" of the school. The people in the Pretty Committee were Massie, Alicia, Dylan, Kristen, and the new girl Claire. They are all supposedly beautiful besides Claire. She wears ugly clothes, has greasy bangs that go straight across her forehead, and an awful since of fashion. Throughout the previous books, the Pretty Committee go on a and off with liking Claire. They are pretty much forced to be with her non-stop because her family lives in Massie's guesthouse. it was only a temporary move because Claire was just staying there until their family could get the Claire's dad a new job. Then they would be able to afford a house of their own. Massie and Claire become really close after a while and Massie starts to think of Claire as her sister. When Claire's family decides to move back to Chicago, Massie and Claire are crushed. They Finally convince Claire's dad to let them stay. Massie and Claire hang out a lot so when they went to a party together they met Alicia's cousin that was originally from Spain. She is stunning with beauty and all the the Pretty Committee's boyfriends like her. Her name is Nina. Nina acts really nice and innocent but she secretly is trying to steal all of the girls' boyfriends. I liked the book a little but i thought the point was pretty stupid. I really like Claire because she is sweet to everyone and is not the least bit self-centered. Massie is probably my favorite character, because she is really cool and has a great since of fashion. Everyone likes her at the school. I don't like Kristen and Dylan because they think they are "all that". They are really sassy. I hated Nina because she was just self absorbed and was just plain rude. I really like Alicia because she is really pretty and has a lot of friends. She isn't only friends with the Pretty Committee; she is also friends with others outside of the group. It makes her seem a lot less Cliquey than the other girls. I recommend this book to girls because it talks about girl things a lot. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13465598357320184505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337027845?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Norby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Norby" href="/user/show/59440653-jacob-norby">Jacob Norby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337027845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13225880047985976974">Personal Response<br/>This book is absolutely awful. I've never read a book that has made me so angry. Every sentence in this book is pure agony. Usually I am able to somewhat relate with book characters, but here I just despise all of them. The writing is also pretty bad; it does a terrible job at explaining what's happening so it's kind of hard to follow.<br/><br/>Plot Summary<br/>Massie is a 12 year old girl who wants to be the most popular and pretty girl in the school. She also has a few friends friends that a</span>
  <span id="freeText13225880047985976974" style="display:none">Personal Response<br />This book is absolutely awful. I've never read a book that has made me so angry. Every sentence in this book is pure agony. Usually I am able to somewhat relate with book characters, but here I just despise all of them. The writing is also pretty bad; it does a terrible job at explaining what's happening so it's kind of hard to follow.<br /><br />Plot Summary<br />Massie is a 12 year old girl who wants to be the most popular and pretty girl in the school. She also has a few friends friends that are part of the "Pretty Committee." Another one of her friends named Claire had to temporarily move in with her. Then this girl named Nina moves in to their school from Spain, and all the boys fall for her. Obviously the rest of the girls aren't happy about this since their boyfriends are all staring at Nina. So the girls decide to get revenge on Nina for taking their boys.<br /><br />Characterization<br />All the character's are pretty much the same bland popular girl stereotype. They don't learn anything throughout the story. The author could have easily made the girls learn something by the end of the book, but that didn't happen.<br /><br />Recommendation<br />This book is meant for bratty 12 year old girls who want to read about what they wish their lives were like. I don't fall into that demographic though so I don't know if my opinion matters. Personally I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1217127129" />
    <a title="Emma Eckel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38963609-emma-eckel"><img alt="Emma Eckel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425594944p2/38963609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1217127129?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Eckel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Eckel" href="/user/show/38963609-emma-eckel">Emma Eckel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1217127129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer618464439514911095">What would you do if you were queen bee? If you had the whole school in the palm of your hand? Massie Block has just that and she's not about to let it slip away. Especially not to Alicia's cousin from Spain, Nina. Nina is Massies biggest competition and all the boys seem to love her. Massie is going from the "it" girl to just second best and she won't stand for it, Nina has to go. Ever since she showed up from Spain she's been taking things that aren't hers; Massies friends, boyfriend, and Goss</span>
  <span id="freeText618464439514911095" style="display:none">What would you do if you were queen bee? If you had the whole school in the palm of your hand? Massie Block has just that and she's not about to let it slip away. Especially not to Alicia's cousin from Spain, Nina. Nina is Massies biggest competition and all the boys seem to love her. Massie is going from the "it" girl to just second best and she won't stand for it, Nina has to go. Ever since she showed up from Spain she's been taking things that aren't hers; Massies friends, boyfriend, and Gossip Girl lip gloss. The question is how? How does Massie terminate her threat? With the help of her friends, Alicia and Claire, they brainstorm a brilliant plan to knock Nina down, so they can climb to their rightful positions at the top. <br />I wanted to read this book because I've already read the first three and I adored them all. I really like this book because these girls dress in a lot of designer brands that I know about and it's pretty cool to be able to be able to make that connection and think "Hey I have a purse from there" or "I went shopping there a few times". I definitely recommend this book for girls who love petty drama. It's a fairly fast read, I finished in within a day or two. This book really isn't for guys, it's more of a girly girl book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="618464439514911095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756802315" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13194907429990848615">This book was amazing! Massie has an upper class life, with her own sized mannequin,(for her and her dog). When her and her pretty-committee are living just fine, Claire, an old family friends daughter, moves into Massies bedroom, and disrupts everything! From going from an annoying person whom she is stuck to be with, to being the person she ditches her friends to be with her. To make it even more dramatic, Alicia, Massies BFF, brings in her cousin from Spain who recently looked like a geek in </span>
  <span id="freeText13194907429990848615" style="display:none">This book was amazing! Massie has an upper class life, with her own sized mannequin,(for her and her dog). When her and her pretty-committee are living just fine, Claire, an old family friends daughter, moves into Massies bedroom, and disrupts everything! From going from an annoying person whom she is stuck to be with, to being the person she ditches her friends to be with her. To make it even more dramatic, Alicia, Massies BFF, brings in her cousin from Spain who recently looked like a geek in all of the pictures, and takes away all of their crushes, who were on the brink of being their boyfriends, and swoons them all. When sabotages go wrong, and she becomes ever MORE popular than she already is, the girls will do anything to stop her. Will Massie, Kristen, Dylan, Alicia, and Claire get back their boys, or will they be thrown out like Massie's month-old clothes? I definitely recommend to girls in Middle School and up, and this book is definitely a must read if you like girls books with drama and humor. There is a series made up of 14 books and have been continuing to read every one!</span>

<div id="review_2213490857" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2213490857" />
    <a title="Avary Gish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71363163-avary-gish"><img alt="Avary Gish" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2213490857?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Avary Gish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Avary Gish" href="/user/show/71363163-avary-gish">Avary Gish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2213490857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13195553328246913371"> The last book I read was Invasion of the Boy Snatchers by Lisi Harrison. This book is about a couple of young girls who have an unexpected visitor. Not knowing that she had changed so much, they didn't really think too much of it. Until they saw her, then things changed. The most popular one who just got her friends back was now being challenged. Which had only happened once, and didn't turn out so good. So just when their lives where starting to look up for them she had to come and ruin it. Sh</span>
  <span id="freeText13195553328246913371" style="display:none"> The last book I read was Invasion of the Boy Snatchers by Lisi Harrison. This book is about a couple of young girls who have an unexpected visitor. Not knowing that she had changed so much, they didn't really think too much of it. Until they saw her, then things changed. The most popular one who just got her friends back was now being challenged. Which had only happened once, and didn't turn out so good. So just when their lives where starting to look up for them she had to come and ruin it. She was much different from before and was even trying to get the other girls boyfriends to fall for her. Which of course made them mad, since they were finally starting to click. Now, they were getting more and more worried. But after time had passed and she had left, things could finally start getting back to normal. Which they did, and it all worked out in the end. Things were even better than before.<br /><br /> I did and did not like this book. I didn't like this book because I feel like it was more grown up for being more of a kids book. I didn't like how they added the very grown up girl, and all of her "experiences" with guys. But I also feel like a lot of girls in middle school can relate to that. Definetly more girls than guys will be able to, but it still sends an important message. I know that I definitely felt a connection while reading the book since I have experienced mean girls. The boys part I can't relate to much though. I feel like that part was way more grown up. But other than that I really did like this book. As far as the actual book goes, I think that it was really well written and I would read it again. I just feel like they didn't need to add some of the things that were in here, but I understand that some things should be said to get the point across. Besides that though I really loved the book. <br /><br /> I would definitely recommend this book. I would recommend it because It is very original yet a lot of girls could make a connection. I know that these books aren't for everyone, but I didn't think I would like them at first and now I love them. I would also recommend them because as you read each book you get to really know the characters each more so you understand and love the books more. I feel like the content of this book is meant more for 7th and 8th graders though. I think this because as I said before, these books are more grown up and meant for older girls. I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone in elementary school because of the content. But like any book there are many pros and cons. Other than that this book is really amazing and I would recommend it many times.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13195553328246913371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926497452?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie Atkins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie Atkins" href="/user/show/59366719-jackie-atkins">Jackie Atkins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926497452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11219492226459671829">The main characters in this book are, Claire Lyons, Nina Callas, and Massie Block. It takes place in Westchester, New York. The story is mainly held on the school grounds of Octavian County Day School, or as the girls call it “OCD”. OCD is an all girls school and the all boys school is called Briarwood Academy. The main conflict in this book is that winter break is over and all the girls just got back to school from their winter vacations. One of Massies best friends, Alicia, was visiting her fa</span>
  <span id="freeText11219492226459671829" style="display:none">The main characters in this book are, Claire Lyons, Nina Callas, and Massie Block. It takes place in Westchester, New York. The story is mainly held on the school grounds of Octavian County Day School, or as the girls call it “OCD”. OCD is an all girls school and the all boys school is called Briarwood Academy. The main conflict in this book is that winter break is over and all the girls just got back to school from their winter vacations. One of Massies best friends, Alicia, was visiting her family in Spain and brought her cousin, Nina, back to Westchester. Nina is going to school with Alicia and the girls do not like her. She is very pretty and outgoing, and is stealing Massie and her friends spotlight. Massie used to be the most popular girl at OCD until Nina showed up, now all of the girls are obsessed with Nina. All of the boys from Briarwood are all over her as well, and Massie and her clique are not happy about it because she is stealing all of their “boyfriends” away from them. I really enjoyed this book, along with the rest of the series. I like that the struggles the girls go through are real life situations. Another thing I enjoy about this book is that Claire and Massie become really good friends, unlike the other books in the series where they are enemies. One thing I didn’t like was that the girls can be kind of cruel to each other and it can sometimes get out of hand. I suggest this book to readers who enjoy drama, and reading about the struggles of teenage girls. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2766693330" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2766693330" />
    <a title="Priscilla King" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67528820-priscilla-king"><img alt="Priscilla King" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2766693330?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Priscilla King" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Priscilla King" href="/user/show/67528820-priscilla-king">Priscilla King</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2766693330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3627285241200670922">This is a comedy series where the joke's on the middle school girl characters. Massie, the mean girl who calls herself and her friends "The Pretty Committee" (pretty is as pretty does, and they <i>don't</i>), is the sort of person a sensible seventh grade girl would avoid even if their fathers work together. Claire, however, wants to be in a "popular clique" of girls who are not so much richer, prettier, or better dressed than their classmates, but meaner, better at making others feel left out and ther</span>
  <span id="freeText3627285241200670922" style="display:none">This is a comedy series where the joke's on the middle school girl characters. Massie, the mean girl who calls herself and her friends "The Pretty Committee" (pretty is as pretty does, and they <i>don't</i>), is the sort of person a sensible seventh grade girl would avoid even if their fathers work together. Claire, however, wants to be in a "popular clique" of girls who are not so much richer, prettier, or better dressed than their classmates, but meaner, better at making others feel left out and therefore want to be let in. So she actually wants Massie as a friend, and now they are, nominally, friends--for whatever that's worth, where Massie's concerned. In this volume they're distracted from their little social dominance displays by a new classmate from Spain who seems a bit older and flirts more shamelessly than they do. These girls are at the age where they only want "boyfriends" as proof of popularity, but while they're making bets about who will and won't be kissed at the dance, Nina the outsider is telling the boys that kissing girls brings bad luck in sports--just so the Pretty Committee won't win their bets. <br /><br />It's all just harmless age-appropriate sneering at the sort of girls who form middle school cliques, but I'd be concerned about a middle school girl who read one book in this series and wanted the others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3627285241200670922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11232041559707624916" style="display:none">This book yet again left me speechless like the rest of the books in the series! It always brings me into the book and makes me feel like I am actually there. Lisi Harrison developed the characters so well that I found myself getting angry or really happy when events happen to the characters. They had so many plot twists that kept tying me in more than I was before. This series will never disappoint me. They have really realistic scenarios and touch on topics that a lot of teens, including myself, deal with. Overall I recommend this book and series to any teen or young adult. It is really intriguing and interesting, not to mention funny. So, if you are looking for a book that is light-hearted and full of interesting drama you should definitely read this series.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9690142291049169371">It was definitely not the best in the series. It wasn't the worst book in the world, but it was definitely not my favorite book in the series. Firstly, they kind of exposed Nina in a bad way. They could've just confronted her instead of humiliating her in front of the entire school. Secondly, I hated the plot. Why are all of them so obsessed with kissing? Who cares? Lastly, the ending was a total bust for me. It ended on a bad note and left me wondering about how Cam and Claire were gonna end up</span>
  <span id="freeText9690142291049169371" style="display:none">It was definitely not the best in the series. It wasn't the worst book in the world, but it was definitely not my favorite book in the series. Firstly, they kind of exposed Nina in a bad way. They could've just confronted her instead of humiliating her in front of the entire school. Secondly, I hated the plot. Why are all of them so obsessed with kissing? Who cares? Lastly, the ending was a total bust for me. It ended on a bad note and left me wondering about how Cam and Claire were gonna end up as a couple. I really hope the 5th book will not be as disappointing as this on was.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dj7Q3Sj7GUilnIX+ZEV7sy5l+kNuYePz631p4LXt2RhhvyOLkPiKS9MFWqiuHUxvJEVJPCkINgZVBUkUGU9EXQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zanKMJfuOajkTU5vEtG2M3sM2dF/JQrE7U4jCHkpoI7aKDlmL+2qq5LUkTnYiYHvcSxqrjhM3zFTNgP81Ys9yw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1106986033218959050"><i>Lisi Harrison</i> is the author of the #1 New York Times best-selling series "The Clique", "Alphas", "Monster High," Pretenders," and her first adult novel: "The Dirty Book Club" out 10.10.17. Lisi was born in Toronto, Canada, and lived in NYC for 15 years while she worked at MTV. She now lives in Laguna Beach, CA and is a member or her own Dirty Book Club. <br/><br/><br/><br/></span>

</div>
